(core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/Server.scala) as the top-level interface, defining `startup()`, `shutdown()`, and `awaitShutdown()`. The `Server` object also defines a `ProcessStatus` sealed trait hierarchy with states: SHUTDOWN, STARTING, STARTED, SHUTTING_DOWN.\\n\\nThe `KafkaBroker` trait (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/KafkaBroker.scala) extends this for broker-specific lifecycle.\\n\\n**Startup ordering** (in KafkaRaftServer.startup): The controller starts first (ControllerServer.startup), then the broker (BrokerServer.startup). This ensures controller endpoints are ready before the broker registers.\\n\\n**Shutdown ordering** (reverse of startup): BrokerServer.shutdown() orchestrates an explicit ordered teardown: (1) stop accepting new connections (socketServer.stopProcessingRequests), (2) shut down request handler pool, (3) shut down kafkaScheduler early to prevent concurrent background tasks from accessing resources being closed, (4) shut down transactionCoordinator, groupCoordinator, shareCoordinator, (5) shut down replicaManager, (6) shut down alterPartitionManager and forwardingManager, (7) shut down logManager, (8) close remoteLogManager, (9) shut down quotaManagers, (10) finally shut down socketServer fully, (11) close lifecycleManager, then call sharedServer.stopForBroker().\\n\\nKafkaRaftServer.shutdown() shuts down broker first (since the controller is needed for controlled shutdown), then controller.\\n\\n**SharedServer** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/SharedServer.scala) uses a reference-counting pattern with `startForBroker`/`startForController` and `stopForBroker`/`stopForController` — shared components (RaftManager, MetadataLoader, SnapshotGenerator) only stop when both the broker and controller have stopped.\\n\\n**BrokerLifecycleManager** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/BrokerLifecycleManager.scala) tracks the broker's KRaft state machine: STARTING → RECOVERY → RUNNING → SHUTTING_DOWN, handling registration with the controller and periodic heartbeats.\\n\\nOn the Java side, the `Scheduler` interface (server-common/.../util/Scheduler.java) and `ShutdownableThread` (server-common/.../util/ShutdownableThread.java) provide base abstractions. `KafkaScheduler` implements `Scheduler`. `NodeToControllerChannelManager` is an interface with startup/shutdown. Services like `GroupCoordinator`, `ShareCoordinator` (in group-coordinator and share-coordinator modules) declare `startup()`/`shutdown()` in their Java interfaces with implementations in `GroupCoordinatorService` and `ShareCoordinatorService`. `LogCleaner` and `RemoteLogManager` also implement startup/shutdown. `KafkaRaftClientDriver` extends `ShutdownableThread` to drive the Raft client loop.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1679,"cache_read_input_tokens":47048,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":1679,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":8,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"04716437-68c4-42c7-a4cf-84d7c5b56c69","uuid":"5efe1651-2d2c-4ebc-8486-93ddd96d5939"}
